Usually, traps are categories that seem plausible but are not intended. For example, in many Connections puzzles, there is a trap of "words that can be preceded by 'go'" but actually those words belong to different groups. The trap set must have exactly four words, drawn from the 16, that form a convincing category but is not one of the real groups. And the trap never takes 3 of its words from a single real group. But we need toascertain if the puzzle's intended solution includes that trap. Usually, the trap is something that many solvers might mistakenly group, causing them to fail. The "-er" trap is plausible because many solvers might see RAP, JAZZ, CALL, READ and think "add -ER" category. However, would they think of that before seeing the other groups? Possibly. But the ghost group is very obvious (SPECTER, SHADE, SPIRIT, WIGHT). The music group is also obvious (RAP, JAZZ, AMERICANA, CHORAL). The predict group is also somewhat obvious (FORECAST, DIVINE, READ, CALL) – though "READ" and "CALL" might be less obvious, but "FORECAST" and "DIVINE" strongly hint at "predict". The break group (BLEW, BURST, BROKE, SPLIT) is also fairly obvious as synonyms for "burst" or "break". So a solver would likely find these four groups quickly. The "-er" trap would be less obvious because you need to think of adding -ER. However, some solvers might see RAP, JAZZ, CALL, READ and think of "words that can be verbs" but that's too broad. The "-er" category is more specific. But would a solver think of that before solving the other groups? Possibly not. However, the trap is designed to be convincing, meaning many solvers might be tempted to group those four together, leaving the remaining words not forming coherent groups. But if they group RAP, JAZZ, CALL, READ as "-er" words, the remaining words would be: SPECTER, SHADE, WIGHT, SPIRIT, BLEW, BURST, BROKE, SPLIT, FORECAST, DIVINE, AMERICANA, CHORAL. That's 12 words. Could they form three groups of four? Possibly: ghost group (SPECTER, SHADE, SPIRIT, WIGHT) – that's one. Break group (BLEW, BURST, BROKE, SPLIT) – that's second. Then remaining: FORECAST, DIVINE, AMERICANA, CHORAL. That's not a coherent group. "AMERICANA" and "CHORAL" are music, but "FORECAST" and "DIVINE" don't fit. So the solver would be stuck. Thus the "-er" trap would indeed make the puzzle unsolvable if chosen. And it uses two words from music group and two from predict group, satisfying the trap rule (no three from one group). HOW TO PLAY 1. You are given 16 words that form 4 hidden groups of 4 related words each. 2. Sort all 16 words into the 4 groups they belong to. 3. Every word must be used exactly once. Each group must contain EXACTLY 4 words. BONUS Some puzzles hide a TRAP: a 5th set of 4 words, drawn from the same 16, that forms a convincing category but is not one of the 4 real groups. Playing it as a group would leave the puzzle unsolvable, because its words actually belong to different real groups. If a trap exists, identify its 4 words. A trap never takes 3 of its words from a single real group. SCORING This is a One-Shot Puzzle. You get to submit your response exactly once with no feedback. Base: 1 point per matched group; a perfect solve (all 4 groups) scores 3. Trap bonus: - +2 if your trap set is a genuine designed trap. - +2 if you state N/A and the puzzle truly has no traps. Maximum: 5 points per puzzle. If your answer is not in a valid format — not exactly 4 groups of 4 words, or the 16 words do not exactly match the puzzle's words — you score 0.
